MONEY TO BE
PICKED UP
Lawyers Desire to Help
Alameda's Treasury.
WANT HALF OF THE BOOTY
THIBTY THOUSAND DOLLARS
OWED BY THE STATE.
Supervisors Will Hold a Special
Meeting to Consider
a the Matter in
Detail.
Oakland Office San Francisco Call,
SOS Broadway, Aug. 29.
It Is believed there Is a sum of $30,000
duo Alameda County from the State
treasury on account of rebates and other
charges that have not been refunded to
the county. This matter was called to the
attention of the Board of Supervisors by
ex-Judge Nusbaumer on behalf of Messrs.
Rogers, Paterson & Slack of San Fran
cisco, who offered to do the legal work
In return for 50 per cent of all .money col
lected.
District Attorney Church advised the
Supervisors this morning that they had
full power to employ counsel In the man
ner suggested.
Attorney Nusbaumer warned the board
that unless the money was collected be
fore January 1 the Legislature might pass
a remedial statute putting the money out
of the reach of the county. He said the
attorneys he represented would pay all
expenses and do all work for a contingent
fee. The attorney stated that the officers
who have been handling the revenues of
the State in this county have overpaid the
State, but he could not tell just what
money or what amount had been thus lost
to the county.
Supervisor Church thought the plan a
good one. He said the board would be
under no expense in getting the money, j
and If it was due it should be paid back. !
His remarks were supplemented by Mr.
Nusbaumer, who said it would be just like
finding money.
Supervisor Roeth wanted to know why
this money could not be collected by the
District Attorney, to which Mr. Nus- ;
baumer replied that the District Attorney
could, collect the money, but he would
have to be told where to find It.
Supervisor Mitchell said he had been In
formed that there is about $30,000 to be
thus collected, and he thought that $15,w0
was too much to pay the attorneys. He
suggested that vie board meet as a com- j
mittee of the whole and talk the matter
over, and this suggestion was adopted.
Students to Marry.
OAKLAND, Aug. 29.â Fred Hathaway
Blxby of Los Angeles and a former stu
dent at the State University has secured
a license to marry Miss Florence Green
of the class of 1900. The prospective bride
was valedictorian of her class in the Sac
ramento High School two years ago.
A RESERVE FUND.
The 'Woodnien of the World Decide
to Create One for the Pacific
Coast.
The Head Camp of the Pacific Jurisdic
tion of the Woodmen of the World re
sumed business yesterday. At the morn
ing session the subject of creating a re
serve fund for the jurisdiction was taken
up and discussed at great length, Uut be
fore any conclusion was reached the mat
ter was passed until the afternoon.
The proposition to creat a new head
camp officer, that of editor of the Pacific
Woodman, the official organ, published in
Denver. Colo., was taken up. This took
up considerable time, but was finally car
ried and A. B. Keith of Butte, Mont., was
elected to that position.
At the afternoon session the reserve
fund matter was taken up again and the
greatest latitude was given to all dele
gates to express their views. It was de
cided that a reserve fund should be
formed, the vote being almost unanimous.
An adjournment was taken until this
morning.
The Women of Woodcraft were in ses
sion all day yesterday and spent the time
in the discussion of proposed changes in
the constitution, each section being con
sidered separately.
On Sunday the sovereign officers, Head
Camp officers and delegates, together with
the Women of Wooueraft, were taken in
carriages to the park, Sutro Heights,
Sutro Baths and the Cliff House. The
visitors were shown all the objects of In
terest and in the afternoon there was a
banquet at the Cliff at which there were
present 180 persons.

Sullivan Arraigned.
Cornelius J. Sullivan was arraigned In
Judffe Mogan's court yesterday on the
charge of murdering his stepfather, John
C. Pratt, at the latter's residence. 633
Minna street, Saturday night. He pleaded
not guilty and the case was continued till
September 2.

FOR THE UNITED STATES
OF CENTRAL AMERICA
The Federal Congress Appointed to
Draft a Constitution
Adjourns.
Special cable to The Call and the New York
Herald. Copyrighted, 1898, by James Gor
don Bennett.
PANAMA, Colombia, Aug. 29.â The
Herald correspondent in Managua, Nica
ragua, telegraphs that the Federal Con
gress apointed to draft a constitution for
the United States of Central America ad
journed last night.
Elections for the President of the
greater Republic will take place In De
cember. The present Government will
continue its sessions until November 1,
when its powers will be transferred to
Senor Amalpa and a new regime estab
lished provisionally by the constitution.
ACCIDENTALLY SHOT.
San Franciscan Loses His Life While
Hunting Near Napa.
NAPA, Aug. 29.â The body of L. Balart,
a cigar manufacturer of San Francisco,
was found on the Deweers place, about
three miles north of here, last evening.
He had been hunting In the hills, and
evidently had stopped to eat his luncheon,
but seeing game In the brush had started
for It. In going through the brush his
shotgun was discharged. The entire
charge entered the abdomen on the right
side, and, ranging upward, Borne of the
shot lodged In the heart. Death must
have been Instantaneous. A hunter acci
dentally discovered him dead In the brush,
with the shotgun across his legs, one bar
rel discharged. It was an old-fashioned
muzzle-loading gun. A few feet away
was his half-consumed lunch. He had
been dead several hours, but his clothing
was still burning, having been ignited by
the discharge.
Mr. Balart had been in Napa only a few
days, and was representing the Knights
of Honor. He was a native of Spain, 52
years of age, and leaves a widow and
children in San Francisco.

THE SAIST FRANCISCO CALL, TUESDAY, ATJGrTTST 30, 1898.
OPIUM FOUND IN
CANS OE LARD
How the Drug Reached
San Quentin.
AUTHORITIES MAKE A HAUL
RECOVER A QUANTITY OF THE
CONTRABAND ARTICLE.
Was Smuggled in by Convicts Who
Were Made to Work on a Farm
Which Supplies the Prison
With Provisions.
Special Dispatch to The Call.
SAN QUENTIN PRISON, Augr. 29.-
It was only last week that the prison
officials were dumfounded at learning
the true status of the opium traffic
as carried on by the convicts inside
the prison walls. Their eyes were then
opened to a realization of the fact that
the trade in the soul-destroying drug
was not confined to a few of the more
vicious element, but that some of the
"trusties" were engaged in smuggling
goodly quantities of the contraband ar
ticle through the gates and dispensing
it to their companions at exorbitant
prices.
Now come to light the facts as to
how the famous ' 'redroom" discovery
happened to be made, showing what
was hitherto known only to the offi
cials in the "higher circle"â that only
a short time ago the authorities made
a haul of the largest quantity of opium
secured in years. It was a clew that
popped up i*n connection with the seiz
ure that led to the "redroom" raid.
About midway on the road leading
from San Quentin to Greenbrae is sit
uated a large farm, the products o{
which find their way to the prison
larder. It Is in charge of J. Jones,
who is entered on the prison payroll
as "farmer" and has the privilege at
any time of asking for a number of
convicts to assist him in his work.
Shortly before the opium was seized
a number of hogs were butchered and
several trusties assisted in preparing
the meat and trying out the lard. The
lard was placed in the ordinary cans
used for the purpose and sent to the
prison.
Certain peculiar actions of the con
victs in handling these cans led to a
quiet investigation. As a result small
quantities of opium were discovered in
three cans. Nothing was said of the
discovery, and it was decided to let the
opium enter the prison in the hope of
making a large seizure.
The vigilance of the officials was re
warded. The next consignment of lard
was searched and a large quantity of
opium found. There were only two
cans out of thirty that had no opium in
them. The aggregate quantity was
about seven pounds.
All this opium must have been hidden
on the farm by accomplices on the out
side. The accurate movements of the
convicts showed, furthermore, that
they must have been In daily commu
nication with the outside dealers. In
spite of the vigilance of the officials
and guards.
It was by keeping a close watch upon
some of the suspected "trusties" that
the opium was found in the "red
room." Other prisoners are under sus
picion, and it is believed the gang of
"opium merchants" Is in a fair way to
be broken up.

sign and to be constructed of stone or brick,
or of both, with all the latest scientific im-
provements required as to construction and
sanitation, equal to. If not superior, to any
building designed or contracted for hospital
purposes, as are indorsed by medical author-
ity as being indispensable In the construction i
of such a building.
The said hospital building to be erected on
the lot of land selected and approved by the
Board of Health, described ac follows:

CORBETT WILLING
TO MEET McCOY
Will Ask for Another
Postponement.
GOES EAST TO OBTAIN IT
WOULD LIKE TO RETIRE FROM
THE RING FOR GOOD.
Why the Ex-Champion Sacrificed His
Pompadour for a Society Hair-
Combâ His Future
Movements.
James J. Corbett is willing to keep his
fistic engagement with "Kid" McCoy.
Shortly before leaving for the East last
evening the ex-champion made this state
ment, but added that he would confer
with the directors of the Hawthorne
Athletic Club on his arrival In the me
tropolis with a view to having the con
test postponed.
The famous pugilist's happy and rol
licking spirit has been subdued by the un
timely taking-off of his parents. Traces
of grief are still apparent in his counten
ance and his manner of talking tells that
his thoughts are elsewhere.
"If it were not for the fact that these
men have gone to trouble and expense in
preparing for the contest," said Corbett,
"I would call the match off. Personally I
have spent hundreds of dollars for train
ing: but I would not mind losing the
money. Everybody thinks it but proper
that I should give up the business, and
although I feel as they do, there are some
things that one has no control over
"l telegraphed my manager, George
Constantine, to arrange a meeting with
the tMrectors of the Hawthorne Athletic
Club in New York on Saturday night, so
that we all could discuss the postpone
ment of the affair. I am willing that it
go over as long as they will allow, as the
news of my parents' death has been a sad
blow to me. _
"They want the fight to come off some
time between the 25th of Septpmber and
the Ist of October, and if no further delay
can be Had 1 suppose we will meet then.'
Jims attention was called to the change
in his appearance wrought by sacrificing
his pompadour to the latter-day style of
Darting it in the middle. He explained
the loss of the pompadour by saying that
when in training he wore a cap. which
pressed his hair down. When heated, the
hair naturally parted on either side of
his forehead, and on his return from ex
ercfse one night his wife took a comb and
tried parting his locks, with such good
results that he has allowed It to remain
that way. He is now minus the title
"Pomradour Jim."
Corbett Is looking well, despite his usual
sallow appearance. His eyes are clear,
and beneath his dark coat his muscles
show firm and active.
TIRED OF WAITING.
Board of Trade May Soon Move to
16 Post Street.
The directors of the California State
Board of Trade have about decided that
patience under certain circumstances
Is. not a virtue, but that It is nonsensical.
This conclusion has been induced by the
action, or rather inaction, of the State
Board of Harbor Commissioners. When
the exhibit of the Board of Trade was at
16 Post street it was decided to have It
moved to the Mechanics' Pavilion and
become a part of the big mining fair, af
ter which it was to be kept at the Pa
vilion for a few weeks until the new
quarters at the big ferry building should
be ready for its reception. It has been
at the pavilion ever since. Time and
again Manager J. A. Fllcher has been
before the Board, of Harbor Commission
ers asking for information as to when
the exhibit space and office room would
be ready, and each time the answer led
to the belief that the move could be made
before very long. It was particularly de
sired that the exhibit should be installed
while tho soldiers from the East were
here, the belief being that it would at
tract much attention, which would be
heralded all over 'the United States by
admiring warriors.
Very recently more inquiry was made
on the same lines, and as a move to the
depot seems to be as far away as It was
many months ago, the directors have
about decided to move back into the old
quarters at 16 Post street. If such a
move is made the Board of Trade will
be a little slow about making another
change. The place is centrally located,
and when the exhibit was there before it
attracted much attention. Whether or
not this change will be made will be de
cided within a few days.
In Self-Defense.
Juan Gomez was tried by a Jury yester
day in the United States District Court
on a charge of assault with a deadly wea
pon with intent to commit murder upon
the person of A. Anderson, a sailor on
board the American ship Occidental sev
eral months ago. Gomez and Anderson
had a quarrel, in the course of which
Gomez stabbed and seriously wounded An
derson with a sheath knife. Gomez set
up the plea of self-defense and the jury
believed him, for a verdict of not guilty
â¢was rendered.

SOUBRETTE EDITH HALL TOOK A STAR PART.
Judge Kerrigan as the Heavy Tragedian
Won Applause and a Sweet
Smile.
I DASHING young actress. Miss
/\ Edith Hall, played a star role as
/~\ "the claimant," in Judge Kerri
gan's court room yesterday.
Twelve interested men occupied the
front seats and numbers of other male
spectators lined up behind. The
standing room was all occupied.
Two other women besides Miss Hall
were present, one of them Mrs. Er
nestine Kreling, the proprietress and
manager of the Tivoli Opera House.
She was also In the cast, having most
unwillingly assumed the part of "the
fair defendant." The third lady had a
very small role, merely as companion
to the last one named.
The drama opened with Miss Hall in
a determined attitude, demanding her
salary of Mrs. Kreling. She claimed
$225 for three weeks' salary, stating
that she had signed a year's contract
with the defendant, who was to pay
her 175 per week, and was to assign
her only to soubrette parts. After
forty-two weeks of faithful service,
during which time she did her acts
with spirited energy and success, she
was asked to take the part of the
Pasha's wife In the comic opera of
"Fatinltza." It was not a soubrette's
part, not by a little bit.
"I would not take it!" exclaimed
Miss Hall, with flashing eyes. "Never!
The part was stupid and It did not fit.
Who ever heard of a soubrette as a fat
Pasha's wife!"
The juryâ that is, the front row au
ditors â looked sympathetic, and it was
quite evident that the clever little
actress was gaining gTound. The Idea
that she should be a Pasha's wife did

Accused of Having Broken Faith by

and Pocketing the
lh Proceeds.
D. B. Davison of the Klondike Gold
Exploration Company, of Colorado
Spring's, Colo., is under arrest in Seattle
on a charge of felony embezzlement pre
ferred In this city by Henry C. Hall, one
of the directors of the company, at pres
ent a truest at the Palace Hotel.
The warrant for Davison's arrest was
sworn to before Superior Judge Cook on
Saturday by Hall, and in the complaint it
is alleged that Davlson embezzled $4000
belonging to the company. Detective
Harry Reynolds left for Seattle yester
day afternoon with the requisition pa
pers for the return of Davison to this
city.
. In the affidavit sworn to by Hall he
states that In July of last year a num
ber of residents of Colorado Springs
formed a syndicate to prospect for gold
in Alaska, and later incorporated under
the name of the Klondike Gold Explora
tion Company, with a capital stock of
$1,000,000. Davison and Gerald M. King
were selected to go to the Klondike to
prospect for gold for one year, and they
entered into a contract with the company
whereby they were each to be paid $100
per month salary, and between them to
hold one-fourth of tha shares in the com
pany. All the gold obtained by them
was to be paid into the bank to the com
pany's credit.
King and Davison were given $2400 for
their outfit and living expenses, and
King, who was treasurer, got also $600,
the balance of Davison's salary for the
year, Davison's wife drawing the other
$600 from bank in monthly installments.
On March 11 last $2500 additional was
sent to King, and about that time Davi
son located a claim on French Gulch. He
worked the claim and took not less than
$5000 in gold dust from it, and reports

and I was firm. She violated her con
tract and was not entitled to salary,
as she has done nothing since."
Just at this point the heavy trage

rected a sharp fire at the claimant.
He said that soubrettes were only in
the world to amuse men and made
some uncomplimentary remarks con

which called forth a sharp protest
from Miss Hall, and which did not find
favor with the audience.
Experts now appeared upon the
stage. Dramatic Critic Ewer walked
over to the side of Miss Hall. Stage
Manager Lask lined up with Mrs.
Krellng. There was a sharp dialogue
pro and con between the experts.
Miss Hall seemed to have the best of
it.
Finally two tragediansâattorneys
came to" the footlights and engrossed

Mrs. Krellng. He said the case was

any more salary. She had refused a
superior soubrette's part. The Jury
would so decide.
Mr. Regensburger retorted. He was
for Miss Hall. He said: "There never
was a clearer case. Salary' is due and

rior old woman's part was offered and
refused. No soubrette would take it.
The Jury will so decide."

son sold the claim for J20.000 cash and
came to this city with the proceeds on
the steamer St. Paul, arriving here on
July 17. He took a bag of gold dust to
the Mint and minted It In the name of
D. T. Williams, a roommate on the
steamer, receiving $5000 in gold coin.
The coin was taken to the Bank of Cal
ifornia on August 8 and deposited, and
five certificates of deposit, each for $500,
were Issued by the bank in the name of
Mrs. Laura M. Davlson, his wife. Two
thousand dollars in cash was to be paid
to Davlson, but it is not known what was

The company, not having heard from
Davlson, sent Hall to this city to en
deavor to ascertain if anything was
known about him. He arrived here on
August 15, and it was by accident that
he found out that Mrs. Davison was at
the Baldwin Hotel. He called upon her,
but she denied knowing anything about
her husband. Hall was suspicious, and
employed private dotectlves on the case.
They ascertained that Davlson secretly
left the city on August 14. and last Sat
urday he was traced to Seattle.
Hall at once communicated with Chief
Lees, and the Chief wired to the Chief
of Police at that city to arrest Davison
and hold him pending the arrival of an
officer with the requisition papers. The
exact amount of Davison's embezzlement
is not known.
TO REWARD PATRIOTISM.
McKinley Veteran Club Suggests a
Silver Medal for Soldiers and
Sailors of the Late War.
The McKlnley Veteran Soldiers' and
Sailors' Republican Club at a 'regular
meeting last night adopted resolutions
Indorsing the platform of the Republican
State Convention and pledging Its mem
bers to the support of the nominees of
the convention.
The club is composed of ex-Union vet
erans and sons of veterans, and holds
in high appreciation the gallant services
rendered by the men of the army and
navy during the war with Spain. It de
monstrated this appreciation -by declar
ing by resolution last night that at the
next session of Congress there should be
formulated and passed a law authorizing
the Government to present a medal of
silver, suitably inscribed, to each and
every member of the army and navy
that served or was musfered into the
service during the war with Spain, and
remains in or has been honorably dis
charged from service. In case of death
the medal is recommended to be given
to the nearest relative of decedent.
The club also indorsed the name of
I^eon E. Jones as a candidate for Sheriff,
urging that he be nominated by the San
Francisco County Convention.

idity to the heart of the soubrette. As
for the defendant, she sat unmoved.
The lawyers promptly added the
final dispute about costs, and the cur
tain fell on the words, "We claim a
stay of execution for five days."
Miss Hall goes to New York as
soon as she gets her money. "I hoped
to go to-night," she said. "There are
several openings there for me, but as
yet I have not accepted any of them."
BUTT'S FATE
IS ROSENAU`S
Autocrats of the Harbor
on Their Knees.
GIVEN A SHARP REPRIMAND
WILL NO LONGER BE ALLOWED
TO HARASS THE COLLECTOR.
Admonished by the Secretary of
the Navy That This Is
America and Not
Russia.
It is understaood that the letter from
the Secretary of the Treasury last week
to Lieutenant Butt, reprimanding him for
the non-performance of his duty as com
mander of Golden Gate, the cus
toms boat, whs accompanied by a letter
of similar tenor addressed to Federal
Quarantine Officer Rosenau for the high
handed manner in which he hns ignored
the orders of the Collector of the Port.
As a result of this action on tho part
of the department the customs officials
believe they will be enabled to perform
the duties of their respective offices with
out being further harassed by what they
term the dictatorial and Impertinent In
terference of the Federal Quarantine Of
ficer.
Ever since State Quarantine Officer
Chalmers was removed to a more distant
and more agreeable sphere of Influence,
Dr. Rosenau out-Heroded Herod, in fact
out-Chalmered Chalmers in the facility
with which he succeeded in making him
self an obstruction and a nuisance to the
customs inspectors. By misrepresenting
matters to the Treasury Department he
managed to obtain a ruling In his favor
in the matter of a dispute, a few months
ago, but the effect of this ruling was
marred subsequently by a full report pre
pared by Surveyor of Customs Spear and
his chief deputy, Chauncey Moriarlty St.
John, in which all the facts were pre
sented. Butt and Rosenau had stood in
together, so far as appearances went,
and seemed to have formed an alliance
to ha>ve things their own way on the
bay, irrespective of the wishes of the
customs officials. The downfall of Butt's
pride did not precede that of Rosenau by
a very long period of time. An investi
gation was made by the Treasury De
partment on the representations made by
the Surveyor of the Port and the truth
came to light. The caustic letter to Butt
followed, and was accompanied, it Is re
ported, by one addressed to the obstinate
doctor.
The climax was brought about by the
doctor's characteristic action in the mat

ter of the arrival of the Abble M. Deer
ing from Lynn, Mass. The Deering had
no passengers and was destined for St.
Michael. On the way out she stopped at
Bahia. Brazil, where there was some
sickness among the population. She ar
rived in San Francisco Bay on April 17,
of this year, 107 days from Bahla. There
was no one sick on board and the ves
sel was not subject to quarantine under
the statute, which provides, among other
things, that quarantine shall be enforced
on vessels having sailed from an Infected
port within thirty days.
The customs inspectors went on board
and performed their duty. When Rose
nau, who was late learned of their ac
tion, he sent a false and inflammatory
telegram to Washington to the effect that
the Abbie had arrived with several cases
of yellow fever and smallpox, and that
more than 200 persons had died from
those diseases; that the customs officers
had boarded the vessel and taken away
the papers so that the quarantine officer
was unable to perform his duty in the
matter.
When the affair was Investigated by the
authorities it was found there was no
case of disease of any kind on board the
Abbie and that nobody had died on board.
The doctor's explanation that he had in
tended to say that all those diseases and
all those deaths had been at Bahia and
not on the vessel did not avail him. for
it was evident that the intention of the
telegram was to alarm the department
The detection of this misrepresentation
brought down upon his head a stinging
rebuke from the Treasury- Department.
In addition to the complaints filed
against Rosenau were several in protest
against the doctor's action in destroying
several hundred dollars' worth of lemons
and other fruit by fumigating on ship
board without having takfn proper pre
cautions. It is expected that the officials
will have no more trouble from the acts
of Butt and his friend Rosenau.
SECOND WEEK OF THE FAIR.
The Connaughters Out in Full Force
to Study the Map of Ireland.
The map of Ireland was the center of
attraction at the Irish Fair last evening:,
especially to the natives of -Galway,
Leinster and other counties of Connaught,
it being Connaught province night.
In the most popular county contest the
leaders are: Cork, L.eltrim, Dublin, Done
gal, Tyrone, Monohan and Gal way.
Yesterday was school day, and there
were over 4000 children present from the
various public and parochial schools.
Under the direction of Mrs. F. E. Dunne
flax spinning is practically illustrated in
a kitchen of original design representing
a scene in Ireland. Another lrstructlve
feature is the silk looms weaving Irish
Fair silk handkerchiefs and "Remember
the Maine" doylies, which are sold for
the benefit of the fair fund. The ladles
of St. Patrick's Alliance of America are
in charge of this department, with Mrs.
P. D. Mullaney as chairman.
The Band of Ireland booth In charge
of the Martha Washington Circle, A. O.

nagan Mrs. Butters, Mrs. Donovan and

is one of the principal attractions of the

THE PAJARO RAILROAD.
Annual Report Shows a Healthy
State of Affairs.
The Pajaro Railroad Company filed its
annual report with the Railroad Commis
sioners yesterday. The following- shows
the result of operations for the year 1897
1838: Expended in construction, $52,611 14;
for equipment, $11,717 61; total, $64,32S 75.
The total cost of equipment and construc
tion up to the present day amounts to
$395.719 60.
The gross earnings of the year are $87,
600 09, which, minus the operating ex
penses, $3D.1u5 01, leaves a net income of
$48,495 08. Of the gross earnings. $1493 25
represents the passenger earnings and
$86,100 84 the returns from freight traffic.

NOTABLE FEAT
IN SURGERY
Remarkable Operation at
the County Hospital.,
JOHN RENNIE'S FIGHT FORLIFE
CANCER REMOVED UNDER DIF
FICULT CIRCUMSTANCES.
The Hight Half of the Stomach and
Several Inches of the
Large Intestine Cut
Away.
Hereafter John Rennie of 120 Second
street must struggle along with only half
a stomach and several inches less Intes
tines than he began life with. Rennie,
who is 50 years of age. was removed to
the City and County Hospital on the 7th
of the present month, suffering from
what he supposed to be some disorder of
the stomach, but which proved to be a
cancer of large dimensions.
Rennie was first placed In the medical
ward where he remained for several daya
until the physicians could accurately di
agnose his case, and then he was trans
ferred to the surgical ward, for it was
apparent that only an operation of the
most delicate nature could save his life.
Some days were necessary to prepare
the patient for the ordeal, and last Fri
day the surgeons pronounced the condi
tions favorable, and Rennie was placed
on the operating table. Drs. Ellinwood
and Rlxford, assisted by Drs. Trenholtz,
Hoffman and Gibbons, performed the op
eration, or rather xthe double operation,
known to the surgical world as pyloric
tomy and gastroentrotomy.
An incision was made in the abdominal
cavity, and the cancer located at the
junction of the stomach and large Intes
tine, completely surrounding the open
ing. It was found necessary to remove
the entire right half of the stomach as
well as the Intestine for several inches
from the junction, and this rendered im
perative the second operation of gastro
entrotomy. At the point where the first
operation was performed the intestine is
attached to the abdominal wall so tightly
as to be immovable, and It was necessary
to sew up both the stomach and intestine.
Then the surgeons picked up the latter
about six inches from where it had been
severed and where it is movable, and
making an incision there as well as in
the lower part of the stomach, joined the
two artificial openings, thus shortening
the channel something more than a foot
in all The abdominal cavity was then
closed and the patient again placed In his
cot He rallied rapidly and now eats
freely and retains and digests his food,
showing that the wound has healed and
the new channel performing its function.
Yesterday Rennie' s temperature was
nearly normal, and the physicians pro
nounced his chances of recovery- better
than even. ,
While the operation Rennie has under
gone has been performed before, it is
quite rare, and the conditions are neces
sarily such as to make it extremely haz
ardous. In the first place the prox
imity to the solar plexus renders it
exceedingly difficult for the surgeons to
operate without affecting that spot, for
the slightest touch would cause almost
certain death. Then the danger from
peritonitis is great, for the escape of
any of the germs from the open stom
ach into the system would bring on that
complication. But, thanks to the sur
geon's skill, Rennie escaped that dan
ger, and if all continues well he will t>Â«
as hearty as ever in a few weeks.
COMMERCE IN DANGER.
Important Dispatch Sent to the Am
erican-Canadian Commission.
From all appearances something has
happened at the American-Canadian con
ference in Quebec that nas caused some
alarm on the part of certain commercial
bodies In the eastern part of the United
States. The following dispatch was re
ceived yesterday from Boston by Hugh
Craig, president of the local Chamber ol
Commerce:
There Is great danger that the pressure
brc%ught to bear by certain special industries
against any concessions to Canada affecttn*
those interests may defeat commercial reciproc
ity with Canada. Please -wire American Com
missioners now sitting in Quebec, urging that
consideration of special interests will not bÂ«
permitted to prevent the negotiations of a
commercial treaty that shall secure to the
two countries the broadest possible measure of
reciprocity. I'rgently necessary that telegram
be sent at once.
VT. F. ROBINSON,
President Boston Chamber of Commerce.
Neither Mr. Craig nor Secretary Scott
have any idea of the nature of the danger
alluded to, but the president at once sent
this dispatch:
Senator Charles W. Fairbanks. Chairman
United States High Commission, In Conference,
Quebec, Canada: The Chamber of Commerce
of San Francisco urges the United States High
Commissioners that no consideration of special
interests shall be permitted to prevent the ne
gotiation of a commercial treaty with our
Canadian cousins upon the broadest possible
measures of reciprocity. They are our very
best foreign customers, purchasing more per
capita than any ether nation, consuming ex
actly what we manufacture for our own use.
Make the reciprocal arrangements such that
in a few years their own interests shall prompt
them to knook for admission as an integral
part of the United StatÂ«x>.; that the flag may
fly from the Rio Gran.le to the Arcticâ "na
flag one language, one tariff, one Government.
HUGH CRAIG.
President Chamber of Commerce of San Fran
cisco. ______________
CONVALESCENTS' HOME
NEARING COMPLETION
MISS LAURA McKINSTRY TO AS
SUME CHARGE.
I
Large Sums Received by the Red
Cross Society From Outside
States.
The Red Cross Home for Convalescents,
which is now in course of construction at
the Presidio, is nearly finished and it is
expected to be opened on Friday. Miss
Laura McKinstry, the young society
lady who sacrificed her pleasures to the
cause of the sick, will be in charge of
the hospital. According to the leading
ladies of the Red Cross Society she -is
admirably fitted for the position, having
had months of experience at the Chil
dren's Hospital and possessing tact and
executive ability.
Large sums were received by the State
association yesterday from the following
places:
Ladies of Wrights, through Mrs. J. W. Smith.
$72 75- Willow Olen, $15; Beatrice, Neb.. $81 15;
Mendoelno. $1 25; Eureka. $12 50; Sacramento,
$250- Woman's Relief, Yankton. S. D., $14;
Grass Valley, $26 26; Lampoc. $50; Salt Lake,
$il3; Alameda, $1; McCook, Xeb., $122 77; Oro
ville, $30.
The president and ladies of the Red
Cross Society desire to tender their
thanks to Drs. Well, Stafford, McCone
and Kuegler, who so kindly gave a six
weeks' course of lectures to the society's
class of nurses, which were held in the
lecture hall of the Polycllnic. Thanks
were also extended for the use of the hall
and the illustrations used during the lec
tures.
The ladies of Wright, Cal., gave a grand
ball in aid of the society which netted
$72 25.
THE RAILROAD CASE.
The cross examination of Virgil Bogua
was resumed yesterday afternoon in the
United States Court of Appeals. Mr.
Bogue was questioned by Robert Y.
Hayne as to his statements regarding
the cars and other property of the South
ern Pacific Company, but nothing new
wj* s elicited.
Mr Hayne was assisted by Deputy At
torney General Anderson. The Interests
of the railroad corporation were watched
by E S. Pillsbury. Railroad Commis
sioner Hint on was present on behalf of
the commission and had a delightful nap
in his chair.
